<span id="freeTextContainer9527057681836807432">After spending months trawling through some of the worst written books centred ont he zombie theme i still hadn't manged to scratch the itch of needing a good zombie book, then i found zombie fallout. There are too many good things wiping through my mind right now to even begin to know where to begin, lets see, okay, firsty there is Mike the main character, Marks style of writing has brought him to life i have added him to the list of people that if they were real i'd add to my dinner party invi</span>
  <span id="freeText9527057681836807432" style="display:none">After spending months trawling through some of the worst written books centred ont he zombie theme i still hadn't manged to scratch the itch of needing a good zombie book, then i found zombie fallout. There are too many good things wiping through my mind right now to even begin to know where to begin, lets see, okay, firsty there is Mike the main character, Marks style of writing has brought him to life i have added him to the list of people that if they were real i'd add to my dinner party invites, only if he brought henry though. <br />In all seriousness though, mark has done what many other authors fail to do, he brings characters to life, he manages to juggle quite a respectable amount of characters and each one has been written well enough that i feel like i know them, im emotionally attached to them and they make me laugh. He keeps an eye on them all not letting them become props for the man character but real people with there own agenda and lives to lead, the plot is original and yes i know im taking about a zombie book, but read it i bet your zombie nightmares will be infused with a little extra terror. The stlye of writing is quick and easy to read rpoviding enough back story where needed and humour in all the right places. All the things i love in a book. <br />Although i do think it is only fair to warn you once zombie fallout starts you cant escape!!! <br />Esily one of my all time favourite series and most definitly my favourite all time charater, from any book i have ever read <br /></span>

<div id="review_390983341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/390983341" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/390983341?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/15734601-zombie-fallout">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer390983341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7275033764093766822">In a way here I could just scream...and not from horror of zombies. No, I could scream from frustration. I've not been drawn into the midst of the overwhelming flood of movies, video games and of course books revolving around the "zombie apocalypse". I think it can be a good idea, even a workable one, but I've just never found a version of it that drew me in.<br/><br/>This did at first. A pretty good character and a plot that at least isn't a carbon copy of all the others (though I have seen the idea used</span>
  <span id="freeText7275033764093766822" style="display:none">In a way here I could just scream...and not from horror of zombies. No, I could scream from frustration. I've not been drawn into the midst of the overwhelming flood of movies, video games and of course books revolving around the "zombie apocalypse". I think it can be a good idea, even a workable one, but I've just never found a version of it that drew me in.<br /><br />This did at first. A pretty good character and a plot that at least isn't a carbon copy of all the others (though I have seen the idea used before, once by Tom Clancy). Sadly not too far into the novel it begins to bog down with angsty interaction with people falling apart over the necessities of survival and other cliched parts. <br /><br />The different take on zombies here is okay but again didn't work for me (I suppose saying that some point about zombies not making sense to me is a little logic straining in itself...but it didn't seem to hold together within the idea he'd set up. Maybe just me).<br /><br />By the end I was skimming through the book just to finish it up. I guess I keep looking for a ZA book I can get into. Till then I'll just have to satisfied with good looking women shooting down shambling hordes of apparently self replicating zombies. No logic...but watchable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7275033764093766822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('phZfv2l2faNX2Gi7bX9DVGHhA0CyLgq+ris9TnfBwInjeNzT2CRAJ5QyBwobPCzvmIARuUgp/NOFTz8X7Yx1lg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

As the first waves of injured bystanders, Guardsmen, and rioters arrived at hospitals in and around Portland, it became apparent that a deadly new disease had been unleashed on the population. \n\nWhether the virus was naturally occurring or an escaped lab experiment Cade hadn\'t a clue, and he wasn\'t especially concerned until he learned of its unprecedented virulence, unusual method of transference, and the fact that, according to the talking heads on the news, it brought the newly dead back to life, semi-mindless, and with an insatiable desire to feed on the flesh of the living. \n\nArmed with this new information and now seeing the bigger cities such as Washington D.C., New York, and Los Angeles rocked by the rapidly spreading scourge, Cade ignores the volley of contradictory edicts drawn up by the White House and set into motion by FEMA and DHS, dusts off his tools of war, and loads his truck with supplies. Unable to get ahold of Brook and Raven and unwilling to leave them at the mercy of some distant politician\'s inability to hold the nation together, he begins an impossible 3,000 mile journey across a reeling United States with presumably millions of infected in his path and only one acceptable outcome: find Brook and Raven alive-or die trying.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5068141924320331044\"
